The long interruption disrupts smooth brushing of the teeth. 5) blinking LED while charging Due to the absence of the LCD panel, the charging progress is indicated by blinking LED lights. This is the method used by a previous generation of toothbrush. After a while, the LED lights will wear out and stop blinking. When this happens, there is no way to tell whether the toothbrush is charging and when it has a full charge. I hope that Braun would take notice of these short-comings and bring back the previous generation of Trimph toothbrush. +++++++++++++++++++Update - 1/31/2015 One and a half year later, the battery is now gone. It would not hold the charge. I spend 1 whole day charging it up and only get to use the toothbrush for 2 days before the battery is totally discharged. Worse still, the red low charge light does not come on, so I am left with a mouthful of foam when the battery suddenly died. Since I am rotating this toothbrush with my older Triumph which is still going strong, this means that the battery would have lasted less than 1 year if I am using this toothbrush exclusively. I tried to open up the toothbrush to dispose of the battery, but the white cap at the bottom of the handle would not come off. I contacted the P&G customer service and asked them how to remove the cap. I was told to be a responsible consumer and dispose of the battery properly.   143. I've been using this brush for the better part of a month and for the most part, it's identical to the [[ASIN:B004O76DEC Oral-B Professional Care SmartSeries 5000]] I purchased just over a year ago. Overall, it does a great job cleaning your teeth. For those of you using manual brushes that are considering moving up to electric, there is no contest - GET AN ELECTRIC BRUSH! This electric brush will clean your teeth in a manner far superior to any manual brush, and for that matter, much better than certain inexpensive electrics such as the [[ASIN:B0014AI4VM Spinbrush Pro]], which I had been using for a few years prior. Using your favorite toothpaste, The Oral-B will leave your mouth feeling very clean. As with any toothbrush, manual or electric, it is still very important to floss daily. When I floss at night, I notice is that there is less crud left between my teeth when using this brush with it's Floss Action head.. Less, but not none, so DO continue to floss.<br /><br />What I'm torn about is the \\"nanny\\" aspect of this Oral-B 5000 system and the external display.<br /><br />There is a remote external display which stays in radio contact with the brush. It displays a timer, along with a star and a bar for each of four sections of your mouth. The four sections represented are the upper left, upper right, lower left and lower right sides of your mouth. The brush has an internal timer synced with the external display and by default it emits a beep and it pauses every thirty seconds to signal that it's time to move on to the next section. The idea is to spend thirty seconds on each section for a total of two minutes of brushing time. After two minutes at which time you're done with all four sections, the brush beeps, pauses and a smiley face is displayed on the external display. Oh, happy times!<br /><br />I'm torn about this system because I don't need the timer and I don't like the fact that you cannot turn it off. I normally brush for over thirty seconds in each section (and I have my own way of brushing) and I don't like the way the brush pauses to indicate that its time to move on. Even though there are five \\"modes of operation\\" and one of them is 45 seconds per section (deep clean), you cannot set that mode as the default. No, you have to press the mode button five times every time you brush in order to access that mode. Since they go through all the trouble of the external display, why couldn't they make it so you could choose and set your default options?<br /><br />One useful aspect of the external display is that there is an indicator which lights up red when the brush detects that you are brushing too hard (if you're putting too much pressure on the brush). This is something I do appreciate as brushing too hard can really do a job on your gums (especially with a manual brush). Its best to allow the brush head to do its job with light pressure. Having the indicator, which seems fairly accurate, is nice.<br /><br />One nitpick is that you pretty much have to keep the brush charging or it will be sluggish after two or three brushings. The battery indicator is fairly useless as it will still show a full or 2/3 charge when the brush really needs to be charged to avoid it being sluggish. The brush will still run, but it will be sluggish. What I mean by sluggish is that the motor noticeably slows down from its peak output, so you're not going to get the same clean. The battery pack seems to be removable, but I cannot find a replacement.<br /><br />The Oral-B is one well made brush. It's made in Germany, and it feels solid and well-engineered. It should last for years. The Oral-B 5000 system has all the bells and whistles if you desire. But if you can do without the external display, you could go with the less expensive [[ASIN:B008PEMBNC Oral-B Professional Precision 1000 Rechargeable Toothbrush]], which is basically the same brush, but without the external display. It still has the internal 30 second timer which pauses after each section and five modes of operation. It just does with out the external display and the indicator that lights up when you brush too hard. If you can do without that, the 1000 is less than half the price for what is basically the same brush.nd timer which pauses after each section and five modes of operation. It just does with out the external display and the indicator that lights up when you brush too hard. If you can do without that, the 1000 is less than half the price for what is basically the same brush.

  147. I received this toothbrush thru the Amazon Vine program, and reviewed it on the original product page. That page indicates it has been superseded (and therefore won't link) by the one on this page, though they appear to be identical.<br /><br />I started using a [[ASIN:B00240XRUY Oral-B Cross Action Power Toothbrush]] with the AAA battery about five years ago and the hygienist in my dentist's office said there was a noticeable difference in the condition of my teeth and gums. When this one came along on Vine I thought, \\"What a great way to upgrade.\\" After using it a while I can say it was a worthwhile move.<br /><br />As I take it out of the box, I notice it has a quality feel to it. I note it is made in Germany. It came with one \\"Floss Action\\" brush head.<br /><br />So What's to Like?<br />The charging base can be kept separate from the brush head holder. If you are short on counter space, as I am, this is a handy feature. Mrs. Boilermate doesn't care for any power brush, so the extra head holder is extraneous.<br /><br />Easy to use. I think it is well balanced, and it fits my ham hand quite well. Use too much pressure, and the handle and monitor light up red. It easily rinses clean when I am done.<br /><br />Of course it is louder than a manual brush, but it is quieter than the Cross Action. It has a smoother and more pleasant sound as well.<br /><br />The Cross Action buzzes your teeth as it cleans. This one cleans without feeling like it's going to vibrate your fillings out. The brush head feels softer but it feels like it is cleaning better.<br /><br />I like that the brush beeps and pauses briefly every 30 seconds as a reminder to move on to the next quadrant. It is designed so that you get used to brushing for the dentist recommended two minutes, but after the fourth quadrant it merely pauses and then continues running. It doesn't shut off when you two minutes are up, a plus IMO.<br /><br />The included monitor counts up the time while you brush and shows you which quadrant you have completed. It also shows which program you selected, and shows the time when you're not using the toothbrush. The monitor may be useful if you have children and you're trying to teach the proper way to brush the teeth. They may like the smiley face and the stars that light up as they complete each quadrant. The monitor can be stored on the shelf or mounted on the wall using a holder that supplied with the kit.<br /><br />The travel case makes it easy to take this when I travel.<br /><br />What's Not to Like?<br />If you do need the extra heads, the holder takes up valuable counter space. It cannot be wall-mounted. Stored flat, the heads cannot drip dry as well, especially with the cover over them.<br /><br />The replacement head cost. At over six bucks apiece, you could buy a whole new Cross Action brush for the cost of one refill head for this. And this kit only comes with one. If you have a family that uses this, the costs can add up very quickly.<br /><br />The Next to Bottom Line<br />Do we need this appliance? No. In the same sense we don't need a power mower to mow the lawn. A push type reel mower will cut the grass but it really doesn't do as good a job as a power mower. My dentist has told me for years that a power brush does a better job cleaning your teeth than a manual one.<br /><br />The Bottom Line<br />If it were my own money, would I buy the Oral B Professional 5000, or consider the [[ASIN:B003UKKHB4 Oral-B Professional 3000]] which has the same basic features but with fewer bells and whistles? If I had children I would probably consider this model. The visual guides on the monitor are good teaching aids. Since I don't, and considering I would be the only one using it, I would probably save about 30 bucks and opt for the 3000.<br /><br />UPDATE 1/17/13<br />I still really like this toothbrush, but...It turns out the monitor is a battery hog. I put two fresh alkaline batteries in the monitor when I received it in June of lastyear, and this week they are dead. Since the brush unit still works as before I don't think I will bother to replace them. This only confirms my comments above...I don't feel there is sufficient added value to justify the higher price this model commands over the Professional 3000.

On the Triumph series, moisture would collect at the base, and it would get gross without regular cleaning. This holder is a much simpler design that prevents accumulation, and that's way easier to clean.<br /><br />Speaking of cleaning... if you use any sort of restorative toothpaste (e.g. [[ASIN:B004TL900M Sensodyne Pronamel]]) you absolutely MUST make sure that the motor is clean after each use. Otherwise, the minerals will accumulate around the base, and the pressure sensor will break.<br /><br />And since I'm giving out tips, getting replacement heads on Subscribe & Save is a deal and a half, compared to any store I've been to. It doesn't hurt to have a couple additional packs sent when they're cheaper than usual, too.<br /><br />Going back to welcome design changes, Oral-B has got away from the massive Braun plug that they used on previous models (and still use on Braun shavers) and instead uses a normal North American plug.<br /><br />All things being equal, there's usually some sort of rebate going on high-end Oral-B products, and if you can pick this up for less than a Benjamin, you'd do well to get in on that deal. Capitalism at it's finest.<br /><br />The product itself is sound, but just be aware that you're purchasing something with a battery that will eventually fail. The customer service is very difficult to get in touch with and again, the process of getting this thing fixed is going to be a real pain. I'm probably going to end up just buying another electric toothbrush butI can say with certainty that it will NOT be an Oral-B or Braun toothbrush.   537. Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean + Floss Action Precision 5000 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush<br /><br />I purchased a Precision 5000 earlier in the year, and this Precision 5000 is quite different. First, the packaging has been improved - it is now similar to Amazon's Frustration-Free packaging and most likely better for the environment due to less plastics.<br /><br />The new Precision 5000 has an updated SmartGuide that uses stars to indicate which quadrant you're brushing (or supposed to be brushing) along with a smiley face that is always on with the clock. So at the end of a 2 minute brushing session, there will be 4 consecutive beeps which can get annoying.<br /><br />The brush head interface remains the same, so the existing inventory of brush heads will work on this model.<br /><br />There's still no way to set it to default to sensitive mode. Oral B now requires you to do an extra press of the mode button to get into the sensitive/feather mode (2 total) versus 1 with the older 5000.<br /><br />Overall: 5/5 stars, still the same great Precision 5000 but with some minor tweaks. I wouldn't call it revolutionary or evolutionary, it's just different from the earlier 5000. The SmartGuide seems unnecessary, as are the pauses and beeps every 30 seconds.

Oral-B uses standard heads and chargers throughout their product line so this makes all my old accessories compatible -- a good thing. A good manual (written in clear English) is included along with the brush and accessories (with the former... gasp... actually being made in Germany.) A two year warranty (good) and a 60 day money back guarantee are included.<br /><br />This model comes with a charger, one head, a traveling case and a separate wireless smart guide unit. The cleaning modes for the brush are Daily Clean, Deep Clean, Sensitive, Whitening, and Massage. I am sure all these modes are fine, but 98 percent of the time I use \\"Daily Clean.\\" The SmartGuide takes some explaining. This is a small wireless device (comes with optional wall mount and 2 AA batteries) that is basically a timer for your brush cycles. When you activate your toothbrush it sends a signal to the SmartGuide and shows how long you have been brushing your teeth and with the use of multiple icons how well you have been doing. If you are using too much pressure, a red light appears on both the brush and the guide display -- I found that I was brushing hard way too often so this has been a helpful feature for me. Not sure if harder brushing actually hurts my oral health, but definitely makes the brush heads wear out faster. The SmartGuide works as a normal digital clock for your bathroom.<br /><br />The brush automatically beeps (in the daily clean cycle) every 30 seconds to indicate when the recommended two minute brushing time is complete and the SmartGuide has a large quadrant icon showing the stages of brushing. I laughed when I saw the device and thought it was gimmicky, but now I am hooked and watch the screen. The toothbrush also has its own battery indicator (3 levels) -- most other models only indicate if the battery needs to be charged (like immediately!). I am getting about 10 days of use (2x/day=20 brushings) as described -- though I expect that to diminish as the unit ages as rechargeable batteries aren't good forever (and are NOT replaceable despite the fact they are removable.)<br /><br />A middle-of-the-road Oral-B toothbrush is probably fine for most folks, but if you catch this model on sale or with a rebate it should be a brush that your dentist is happy about you using. I find my replacement heads cheapest at the local warehouse store that starts with the letter C. My hygienist never complains about my teeth (in fact I have no cavities period) but gum issues do run in my family -- hopefully with a good oral health plan including this brush I won't have to suffer the same fate as my parents.

However, it's a significant improvement on the old model.<br /><br />It's easy to see right out of the box and after the first charge that it has much more power, which is a welcome change. It holds enough power for at least 8-10 brushings lasting about 3-3:30 minutes each. That's a substantial improvement over the old Triumph, which didn't perform that well even when new. My only complaint in the battery department is that this unit charges even more slowly than its predecessor, which used to recharge overnight. This new one needs to be recharged for the better part of a day if it has been used for several brushings.<br /><br />It does a great job cleaning, and I even found on the day of transitioning from the old to the new model that my teeth felt instantly cleaner with a bit fewer rough spots. I have been very pleased with the cleaning action of the head on the Oral-B design for 6 years now, and since this one works just the same way, though with a bit more power, I'm confident I'll be as happy with this one as with the last. At each of my cleanings, including one I recently had after having used this toothbrush for a number of weeks, the hygienist and dentist always compliment me on how little plaque I have, so that's a compliment to the Oral-B design as well.<br /><br />The build quality is superb. I can't say I have a lot of use for the accessories (though I am thankful for the addition of a hard-plastic travel case) such as the \\"SmartGuide,\\" which really seems to be designed for parents of toddlers who are teaching their kids how to use a toothbrush. I really don't need a count-down (or count-up, depending on your taste) timer to know when I've brushed my teeth enough. Teaching kids to brush, the SmartGuide may have some application, but for my purposes, it is of little more use than as a digital clock. The only other \\"mode\\" I like to shift to brush in is the \\"Plus\\" mode, which gives me 45-second intervals without interruption pauses.<br /><br />The caddy holds 4 separate brush heads for 4 different users, and that may be useful for families with kids who share a bathroom and can, thus, share a power toothbrush body, keeping their brush heads separate (different colored rings are available for each brush head).<br /><br />All in all, I'm very impressed that Oral-B has continued the tradition of quality and performance that I had grown used to over the years with their older power toothbrush, and I am also pleased that they've improved on the performance of the power cells. I thought the old brush was a 5-star product, so I can't see that this one is anything less than a 5-star product either! Highly recommended, and the Amazon.com \\"Frustration Free\\" packaging on this unit is a welcome addition!compliment to the Oral-B design as well.<br /><br />The build quality is superb.   586. This Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean Precision 5000 Electric Toothbrush is an updated version of the Oral-B SmartSeries 5000 Toothbrush. I own both toothbrushes, and here are the differences between the two:<br /><br />- The biggest change is with the on-handle display. The old version had a small display which showed the charge level, in 4 different increments. When the battery was low, the last bar on the screen would blink. You could see the charge level at all times also. With the new version, the display is gone, and has been replaced by LED lights (in 3 different increments). The light is green when charged, and flashes red when the battery is low. One annoying thing about the new version is the LED light turns off when not brushing. So you can only see the charge level while the toothbrush is in use. I prefer the old method where you can see the charge level at all times.<br /><br />- The charging cradle has been slightly improved. The old version had a ring base that the toothbrush fit into. The new one has a smaller base that the toothbrush is placed on. Not a huge improvement, but I like the new one better because it doesn't get your bathroom counter dirty with toothpaste residue. Now you just need to clean the base.<br /><br />- The 30 second notification to move to the next quadrant has changed. Now, there is more of a noticeable stop after each 30 seconds (though it's just a split second).<br /><br />- The SmartTimer now has a star system that rates you on your brushing time. If you go the full two minutes, all four stars will darken (and the smiley face on the display smiles). If you skip out on the time, not all the stars will darken and you won't see the smiley face. This isn't a big deal to me, but may provide positive reinforcement for those who find it hard to go the full 2 minutes.<br /><br />So as you can see, the changes overall are pretty small. If you have a SmartSeries 5000, you probably don't need to upgrade to the new Precision 5000.<br /><br />Overall, the toothbrush performance is still stellar. It provides 5 cleaning modes- daily clean, deep clean, sensitive, whitening, and massage. You also have a variety of tooth brush heads to use. I prefer the Floss Action, but my wife uses the Sensitive one.<br /><br />One thing I have noticed is that you have to be careful with what type of toothpaste to use. Some pastes create a lot more liquid than others while brushing, and you may find it tough to go a full 2 minutes without taking a break to spit it out. I had to do trial and error with a few different brands to see which one I liked (Colgate Total seems to work well).<br /><br />My dentist has seen improvement with these toothbrushes vs. the old SonicCare I used. It will provide you with a bonus star (5-stars in all) if you brush for an additional 30 seconds or more. The best part is, if you brush long enough to get that extra bonus star, you will sometimes (not every time) be greeted with a winking smiley face. Now who wouldn't like that? The Smart Guide also shows you what brushing mode you are using, displays an icon to show you when it is time to replace your brush head, and also has a red (might be dark orange) lighted indicator to warn if you are pressing against your teeth too hard with the brush. There is a rather large LED light on the back of the powered brush handle as well, which flashes brightly if you are applying too much pressure when brushing. I really like the light on the handle, as it prevents the need for the user to keep watching the Smart Guide display (which can sometimes be difficult to see from a distance).<br /><br />The Precision 5000 series toothbrush, like all other Oral-B powered brushes I have used, does a splendid job of cleaning my teeth. My dentist has had nothing but good things to say about my teeth and gums since I started using my Oral-B Triumph several years ago. It provides a comfortable and stimulating scrubbing action to your teeth and gum-line, but isn't overly aggressive to cause discomfort. This scrubbing action does a great job of removing plaque, preventing stains, and the Floss Action heads do well at getting between teeth and removing food particles. The Oral-B Precision 5000 is far from being whisper quiet, so be prepared for a little noise once you switch it on. It is also a little bulky, and has s fair amount of weight to it. I don't find it to be clumsy or heavy at all, and enjoy the solid feel of the handle overall. The handle is waterproof, and has a good rubbery grip surface. My only real complaint about the new Precision 5000 series toothbrush is the pause in brushing every 30 seconds. While I understand the concept behind the physical feedback, to let you know it's time to switch quadrants in your mouth, and that the physical feedback eliminates the need to watch the LCD display for visual indicators, I don't appreciate the interruption in the brushing motion. In fact, every 30 seconds the pause gets longer, so that you can hear this faint little beep that grows in number during each pause. So, after the first thirty seconds you get a very short pause, with a single beep. After another 30 seconds you get a pause twice as long, with two beeps. By the time you get to the fourth pause, it is so long that you just stand there looking at yourself awkwardly in the mirror, waiting for the stupid thing to start brushing again. The engineer that came up with this concept should be slapped silly, in my honest opinion! My wife has a Sonicare toothbrush that provides a really short stutter in brushing action every 30 seconds, which doesn't interrupt the brushing process, but provides enough feedback to alert the user that another 30 seconds has passed. I think Braun (Oral-B) needs to hire the engineer from Sonicare, to redesign their feedback system, which would bring this device closer to being a 5-star product. As it is now, I consider the Oral-B Precision 5000 power toothbrush to be a solid 4 to 4 and ½ star product. It does a great job cleaning my teeth, and I have very few complaints about its style, build quality, or feature set. Cleaning our teeth should be treated as a vital element of one's daily personal hygiene regimen, and I highly recommend the [[ASIN:B008PEMOV6 Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean + Floss Action Precision 5000 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]] as the right tool for the job.rants in your mouth, and that the physical feedback eliminates the need to watch the LCD display for visual indicators, I don't appreciate the interruption in the brushing motion.   715. I've been using electronic toothbrushes for about 15 years now, and at this point, I don't see myself ever stopping. I started off with a Sonicare, and then switched to an Oral B. After about 10 years of using my Oral B, I decided it was time to invest in some newer technology.<br /><br />This new model is fantastic. Every 30 seconds, it gives a little extra buzz to let you know to move to a different quadrant of your mouth. That is extremely useful because it is very easy to spend more time on one part of your mouth than another. After two minutes, it gives a few extra buzzes so you know you're done. It can be very tempting to skimp out on the amount of time dedicated to brushing, especially when rushing in the morning, but this system helps fight those temptations.<br /><br />As far as quality of brushing, this is exactly what I expected from Oral B.
